Often a student of English tries to translate idioms word-for-word, or literally. If you do this, you can end up asking, \"What could this possibly mean?\" This is why idioms are difficult: they work as groups of words, not as individual words. If you translate each word on its own, you'll miss the meaning and in many cases end up with nonsense. \r\n\r\nAs an example, let's take one of the idioms presented in this book: \"out of this world.\" This expression is often used to describe delicious food.
